I didn&#39;t include it on the handout because we didn&#39;t discuss this in lecture or tutorial.\n\nFor your second question, please note that we always define our ADT operations with a first parameter being an object representing the data structure itself. This provides some consistency across the different operations. For both Find and Union, because we say that they take nodes in the data structure as inputs, the operations can be implemented without referring to any other nodes in the data structure (as you&#39;ve pointed out, the &#34;DS&#34; object is unused).\n\nHowever, keeping the DS parameter allows us to do a couple of modifications to this operation that you might like to think about:\n\n1. Add &#34;global&#34; metadata for the disjoint set data structure, like keeping track of the maximum height of a tree, or the number of different disjoint sets.\n2. Change the behaviour of both Find and Union to take in values rather than nodes. This would require some kind of lookup operation on <code>DS</code> to first find the nodes corresponding to the input values, and then performing the node-based operations we&#39;ve discussed. That&#39;s the random variable - it represents the running time of the function (in Question 1, the number of list items visited), as a function of what input was chosen.\n\nThen you want to identify the *outcomes* of this random variable, which are the possible running times. instructors fast. We've put together this list of tips you might find handy as you get started:\n\n1.  <b>Ask questions!</b>\n\nThe best way to get answers is to ask questions! Ask questions on Piazza rather than emailing your teaching staff so everyone can benefit from the response (and so you can get answers from classmates who are up as late as you are).\n\n2.  <b>Edit questions and answers wiki-style.</b>\n\nThink of Piazza as a Q&A wiki for your class. Every question has just a single <b>students' answer</b> that students can edit collectively (and a single <b>instructors\u2019 answer</b> for instructors).\n\n3.  <b>Add a followup to comment or ask further questions.</b>\n\nTo comment on or ask further questions about a post, start a <b>followup discussion</b>. Mark it resolved when the issue has been addressed, and add any relevant information back into the Q&A above.\n\n4.  <b>Go anonymous.</b>\n\nShy? No problem. You can always opt to post or edit anonymously.\n\n5.  <b>Tag your posts.</b>\n\nIt's far more convenient to find all posts about your Homework 3 or Midterm 1 when the posts are tagged. Type a \u201c#\u201d before a key word to tag. Click a blue tag in a post or the question feed to filter for all posts that share that tag.\n\n6.  <b>Format code and equations.</b>\n\nAdding a code snippet? Click the <b>pre</b> or <b>tt</b> button in the question editor to add pre-formatted or inline teletype text. \nMathematical equation? Click the <b>Fx</b> button to access the LaTeX editor to build a nicely formatted equation.\n\n7.  <b>View and download class details and resources.</b>\n\nClick the <b>Course Page</b> button in your top bar to access the class syllabus, staff contact information, office hours details, and course resources\u2014all in one place!\n\n\nContact the Piazza Team anytime with questions or comments at <b>team@piazza.com</b>.
